<rate>4<//rate>< Review>
What a great idea!  It's like renting an office in a big company.

Your private office costs from $600 to $4000 depending on how many people are using it.  The place was modern feeling and some of the rooms especially against the exterior window looked great!

All the offices are divided by windows and there're plenty of community spaces to interact with others to feel like you're not alone.  It also serves as a gym, in that you see others working hard everywhere so it'll keep you motivated and going.

It's in the middle of San Jose downtown so you can walk to San Pedro Square and there are plenty of choices to eat or drink downstairs, but it also comes with a lot of homeless people in the area.  Parking structures next to it was reasonable at $5-6/day.

They really used up every space they could to rent out with thin claustrophobia unfriendly hallways.< /Review>

< review>
Nice co-working space with decent pricing all things considered. Plenty of room to work, offices to rent for more serious businesses, meeting rooms to book, free coffee and beverages on tap, free mouthwash in the bathroom to get rid of coffee breath... And most importantly, fast reliable internet.

<Pics>None<//Pics>< text>
These guys are a wreck. I called looking for a specific tree, which they reported to have. I drove across town to buy it, and was told that, no, the tree I wanted was at their other location on La Sierra, about a mile from where I was when I had called.

So I opened up Google Maps to look for the location on La Sierra, but it doesn't exist on the map. So I went back in to get directions/ address, and they pulled out a handy, pre-printed, laminated map to look at, which they easily could have given me at first. After studying the map, I observed that the La Sierra location is not in fact on La Sierra, but is instead on Campbell. Which they didn't tell me.

So I programmed in the address, and crossed town again, only to find a locked gate and no one around. The place looked closed. After wandering around for 20 minutes, and figuring out that the gate was not actually locked, I found a worker, who informed me that the tree I wanted was at ANOTHER location over off of a different street (Norwood). So I followed him on a quarter-mile walk to the other site, where he escorted me to the tree I had requested... only to find that it was a DWARF version of the tree. They had no standard-size trees in the variety that I had requested.

So after driving across town twice, and wasting 2 hours trying to get what I wanted, they didn't have the thing they told me that they had.

The only reason I'm giving them 2 stars is because the worker who helped me locate the (wrong) tree was helpful and sympathetic, noting that the guys at the Dufferin location often misstate their stock, don't verify availability, and don't give clear directions to customers. So while it didn't help me at all, at least he understood my situation.

This could all have been avoided with some very minimal customer service effort on their part, saving me hours of wasted time, and a lot of driving. But they don't seem to really care about their customers, so I won't be back. I recommend to you that if you want something from them, be very specific with them about exactly what it is that you want, and make sure you ask where you should expect to find it. Otherwise you may end up on the same wild goose chase that I experienced.

Consider yourself warned.</text>

<time>1546721482241< /time><text>I have to get my Menchie's fix every time I'm in Santa Monica!  I love the natural flavor - tastes like regular yogurt with a little sugar stirred in and frozen.  Seems pretty basic, but I like tart crisp flavors.  I live in Boston and everyone wants to sell heavily flavored and ridiculously sweet froyo here; the only place that serves natural flavor in Boston is Pinkberry's.

Anyway, I like the convenience of self-service.  Grab a container, select your flavor from the dozen available, dispense it, add as much or as little toppings as you want, then weigh it and pay.  If you're not sure, just grab a tiny sampling cup, and try as many free samples as you want.  Easy peasy.

The place is very kid friendly, and since it's self-service, there's no problem getting your youngster a squirt of 3-4-5 flavors if they can't narrow it down to two.

The only reason why I can't give this Menchie's a five-star rating is the cleanliness, and service, can be variable.  I have been there when the staff goes out of their way to be friendly and helpful and the place was spotless.  Other times, the table can be sticky and the servers seem to resent even weighing the product and taking your money., much less being courteous.  I don't mind, because I love natural flavor yogurt and the convenience of self-service.</text><Resp>None</Resp><user_name>Larry Stuart< /user_name><pics>None<//pics>< Gmap_id>

<review>Great service and friendly staff! I do recommend some of the doctors there. The office is clean, and the staff will patiently take their time to answer all of your questions. Their management of paperwork is much better than some other places I have been to. Everything gets done in a timely manner, and they will keep you updated as to the progress of your pet.

However, beware of the bait-and-switch tactic: Sometimes, they'll give you a price over the phone, but when you get there, it's much more expensive! This was done to me twice. So, get the name of the person that quoted you.

Also, another tactic that was done by a doctor to me (I forgot her name) added another service to one of my dogs without even asking me! Extra cash for her I guess.

Overall, I do like and would recommend this place to my neighbors. Just beware of your pocket book. Some doctors are honest with pricing. But others can act like car  mechanics. Sorry, I'll have to get the names of the good ones later.< /review><resp>None</resp>< Name>

< Review>
Really great facility. Vets here are quite knowledgeable (especially Dr. Hess and Dr. Cork). Dr. Malo is great as well. Staff are friendly and personable, treating me more like my neighbor than a customer as they genuinely inquire about my family or other pets when I bring one or the other in. My only complaint is the entire doctor staff take lunch for two hours, makes it a tad inconvenient if ya need to bring your pet in and notice it's close to their lunch break. Another issue I've had is sometimes you really need to push the doctor to investigate an issue. My dog was a stray and I'm not an expert or anything, but when I was given the possibility that my dog might have diabetes I wanted it investigated. The doc downplayed the possibility and took the wait and see approach. I was fine with this, as  the docs don't seem to be the type to rack up bills with every test under the sun, but my dog eventually had a diabetic siezure and an mergency visit to the clinic-which cost a lot more than a damn blood glucose test. Great docs here, but ya still need to be your pets advocate and keep a close eye on things. The doc isn't with your pet day in and out so they may miss things.<//Review>
